# Influenza - Wikipedia

> ## Excerpt
> Influenza, commonly known as "the flu", is an infectious disease caused by an influenza virus.[1] Symptoms can range from mild to severe and commonly include: high fever, runny nose, sore throat, muscle and joint pain, headache, coughing, and feeling tired.[5] These symptoms typically begin two days after exposure to the virus and most last less than a week, although the coughing may last for more than two weeks.[1][6] In children, there may be diarrhea and vomiting, but these are not common in adults.[7] Diarrhea and vomiting occur more commonly in gastroenteritis, which is an unrelated disease sometimes referred to as "stomach flu" or the "24-hour flu".[7] Complications of influenza may include viral pneumonia, secondary bacterial pneumonia, sinus infections, and worsening of previous health problems such as asthma or heart failure.[2][5]

---
Influenza

Other names

Flu, the flu, Grippe

[![EM of influenza virus.jpg](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/EM_of_influenza_virus.jpg/300px-EM_of_influenza_virus.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:EM_of_influenza_virus.jpg)

Influenza virus, magnified approximately 100,000 times

[Specialty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Specialty_(medicine) "Specialty (medicine)")

[Infectious disease](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infectious_disease_(medical_specialty) "Infectious disease (medical specialty)")

Symptoms

[Fever](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fever "Fever"), [runny nose](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhinorrhea "Rhinorrhea"), [sore throat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sore_throat "Sore throat"), [muscle and joint pain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myalgia "Myalgia"), [headache](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Headache "Headache"), [coughing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cough "Cough"), [feeling tired](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatigue_(medical) "Fatigue (medical)")[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2018-1)

Usual onset

One to four days after exposure[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2018-1)

Duration

~1 week[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2018-1)

Causes

[Influenza viruses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza_viruses "Influenza viruses")[\[2\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Harr2012-2)

Prevention

[Hand washing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hand_washing "Hand washing"), [influenza vaccine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza_vaccine "Influenza vaccine"), [surgical masks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surgical_mask "Surgical mask")[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2018-1)[\[3\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Jeff2011-3)

Medication

[Neuraminidase inhibitors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuraminidase_inhibitor "Neuraminidase inhibitor") such as [oseltamivir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oseltamivir "Oseltamivir")[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2018-1)

Frequency

3â€“5 million severe cases per year[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2018-1)

Deaths

Up to 650,000 respiratory deaths per year[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2018-1)[\[4\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2017-4)

**Influenza**, commonly known as "**the flu**", is an [infectious disease](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infectious_disease "Infectious disease") caused by an [influenza virus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza_virus "Influenza virus").[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2018-1) [Symptoms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Symptoms "Symptoms") can range from mild to severe and commonly include: high [fever](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fever "Fever"), [runny nose](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhinorrhea "Rhinorrhea"), [sore throat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sore_throat "Sore throat"), [muscle and joint pain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myalgia "Myalgia"), [headache](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Headache "Headache"), [coughing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cough "Cough"), and [feeling tired](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatigue_(medical) "Fatigue (medical)").[\[5\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-CDC2014Key-5) These symptoms typically begin two days after exposure to the virus and most last less than a week, although the coughing may last for more than two weeks.[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2018-1)[\[6\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Einav2020-6) In children, there may be [diarrhea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diarrhea "Diarrhea") and [vomiting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vomiting "Vomiting"), but these are not common in adults.[\[7\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Dub2011-7) Diarrhea and vomiting occur more commonly in [gastroenteritis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gastroenteritis "Gastroenteritis"), which is an unrelated disease sometimes referred to as "stomach flu" or the "24-hour flu".[\[7\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Dub2011-7) Complications of influenza may include [viral pneumonia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viral_pneumonia "Viral pneumonia"), secondary [bacterial pneumonia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bacterial_pneumonia "Bacterial pneumonia"), [sinus infections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sinus_infection "Sinus infection"), and worsening of previous health problems such as [asthma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asthma "Asthma") or [heart failure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heart_failure "Heart failure").[\[2\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Harr2012-2)[\[5\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-CDC2014Key-5)

Three of the four types of influenza viruses affect humans: Type A, Type B, and Type C.[\[2\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Harr2012-2)[\[8\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-CDC2017Types-8) Type D has not been known to infect humans, but is believed to have the potential to do so.[\[8\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-CDC2017Types-8)[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-InfD2017-9) Usually, the virus is [spread through the air](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Airborne_disease "Airborne disease") from coughs or sneezes.[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2018-1) This is believed to occur mostly over relatively short distances.[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Brankston2007-10) It can also be spread by touching surfaces contaminated by the virus and then touching the eyes, nose, or mouth.[\[5\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-CDC2014Key-5)[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Brankston2007-10)[\[11\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-11) A person may be infectious to others both before and during the time they are showing symptoms.[\[5\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-CDC2014Key-5) The infection may be confirmed by testing the throat, [sputum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sputum "Sputum"), or nose for the virus.[\[2\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Harr2012-2) A number of [rapid tests](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rapid_influenza_diagnostic_test "Rapid influenza diagnostic test") are available; however, people may still have the infection even if the results are negative.[\[2\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Harr2012-2) A type of [polymerase chain reaction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polymerase_chain_reaction "Polymerase chain reaction") that detects the virus's [RNA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RNA "RNA") is more accurate.[\[2\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Harr2012-2)

Frequent [hand washing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hand_washing "Hand washing") reduces the risk of viral spread, as does wearing a [surgical mask](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surgical_mask "Surgical mask").[\[3\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Jeff2011-3)\[_[needs update](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items "Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers")_\] Yearly [vaccinations against influenza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza_vaccine "Influenza vaccine") are recommended by the [World Health Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Health_Organization "World Health Organization") (WHO) for those at high risk,[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2018-1) and by the [Centers for Disease Control and Prevention](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention "Centers for Disease Control and Prevention") (CDC) for those six months of age and older.[\[12\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-CDC2019-20-12) The vaccine is typically effective against three or four types of influenza and is usually well tolerated.[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2018-1) A vaccine made for one year may not be useful in the following year, since the virus evolves rapidly.[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2018-1) [Antiviral medications](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antiviral_drug "Antiviral drug") such as the [neuraminidase inhibitor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuraminidase_inhibitor "Neuraminidase inhibitor") [oseltamivir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oseltamivir "Oseltamivir"), among others, have been used to treat influenza.[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2018-1) The benefit of antiviral medications in those who are otherwise healthy do not appear to be greater than their risks.[\[13\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Mich2013-13) No benefit has been found in those with other health problems.[\[13\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Mich2013-13)[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Ebe2013-14)

Influenza spreads around the world in [yearly outbreaks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flu_season "Flu season"), resulting in about three to five million cases of severe illness and about 290,000 to 650,000 deaths.[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2018-1)[\[4\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2017-4) About 20% of unvaccinated children and 10% of unvaccinated adults are infected each year, according to a 2018 studythr [\[15\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-15) In the northern and southern [parts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_latitudes "Middle latitudes") of the world, outbreaks occur mainly in the winter, while around the [equator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equator "Equator"), outbreaks may occur at any time of the year.[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2018-1) Death occurs mostly in high risk groupsâ€”the young, the old, and those with other health problems.[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2018-1) Larger outbreaks known as [pandemics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pandemic "Pandemic") are less frequent.[\[2\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Harr2012-2) In the 20th century, four major [influenza pandemics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza_pandemic "Influenza pandemic") occurred: the [Spanish flu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_flu "Spanish flu") in 1918 (17â€“100 million deaths), the [Asian flu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1957%E2%80%931958_influenza_pandemic "1957â€“1958 influenza pandemic") in 1957 (1â€“4 million deaths), the [Hong Kong flu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hong_Kong_flu "Hong Kong flu") in 1968 (1â€“4 million deaths) and the [Russian flu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1977_Russian_flu "1977 Russian flu") in 1977 (700,000 deaths).[\[16\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-:1-16)[\[17\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-:0-17)[\[18\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Spreeuwenberg1-18)[\[19\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-TenThings-19)[\[20\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-20) The [World Health Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Health_Organization "World Health Organization") declared an outbreak of a new type of [influenza A/H1N1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza_A_virus_subtype_H1N1 "Influenza A virus subtype H1N1") to be a [pandemic in June 2009](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009_flu_pandemic "2009 flu pandemic").[\[21\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-21) Influenza may also affect other animals, including pigs, horses, and birds.[\[22\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-22)

## Signs and symptoms

Most sensitive symptoms for diagnosing influenza[\[23\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-pmid15728170-23)

Symptom:

[Sensitivity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sensitivity_(tests) "Sensitivity (tests)")

[Specificity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Specificity_(tests) "Specificity (tests)")

Fever

68â€“86%

25â€“73%

Cough

84â€“98%

7â€“29%

Nasal congestion

68â€“91%

19â€“41%

-   All three findings, especially fever, were less sensitive in people over 60 years of age.

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Symptoms_of_influenza.svg/300px-Symptoms_of_influenza.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Symptoms_of_influenza.svg)

Symptoms of influenza,[\[24\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-24)[\[25\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-25) with fever and cough the most common symptoms.[\[23\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-pmid15728170-23)

Approximately 33% of people with influenza are asymptomatic.[\[26\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-AmericanJournalEpidemiology2008-26)[\[27\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-27)

Symptoms of influenza can start quite suddenly three to four days after infection.[\[28\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-28) Usually the first symptoms are [chills](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chills "Chills") and body aches, with [fever](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fever "Fever") also common early in the infection, with body temperatures ranging from 38 to 39 Â°C (approximately 100 to 103 Â°F).[\[29\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-29) Many people are so ill that they are confined to bed for several days, with aches and pains throughout their bodies, which are worse in their backs and legs.[\[30\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Merck-30)

### Symptoms of influenza

-   Fever and chills
-   [Cough](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cough "Cough")
-   [Nasal congestion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nasal_congestion "Nasal congestion")
-   [Runny nose](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhinorrhea "Rhinorrhea")
-   [Sore throat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sore_throat "Sore throat")
-   [Hoarseness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hoarseness "Hoarseness")
-   [Earache](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Earache "Earache")
-   [Muscle pains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Myalgia "Myalgia")
-   [Fatigue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatigue_(medical) "Fatigue (medical)")
-   [Headache](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Headache "Headache")
-   Irritated, [watering eyes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tears "Tears")
-   Reddened eyes, [skin (especially face)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flushing_(physiology) "Flushing (physiology)"), mouth, throat and nose
-   [Petechial rash](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petechia "Petechia")[\[31\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-pmid10476766-31)
-   In children, gastrointestinal symptoms such as [vomiting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vomiting "Vomiting"), [diarrhea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diarrhea "Diarrhea"), and [abdominal pain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdominal_pain "Abdominal pain")[\[32\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Richards-32)[\[33\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-33) (may be severe in children with influenza B)[\[34\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-34)

It can be difficult to distinguish between the [common cold](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Common_cold "Common cold") and influenza in the early stages of these infections.[\[35\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Eccles-35) Influenza symptoms are a mixture of symptoms of common cold and [pneumonia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pneumonia "Pneumonia"), body ache, headache, and fatigue. Diarrhea is not usually a symptom of influenza in adults,[\[23\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-pmid15728170-23) although it has been seen in some human cases of the [H5N1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H5N1 "H5N1") "bird flu"[\[36\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-36) and can be a symptom in children.[\[32\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Richards-32) The symptoms most reliably seen in influenza are shown in the adjacent table.[\[23\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-pmid15728170-23)

The specific combination of fever and cough has been found to be the best predictor; diagnostic accuracy increases with a body temperature above 38Â Â°C (100.4Â Â°F).[\[37\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-pmid11088084-37) Two [decision analysis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decision_analysis "Decision analysis") studies[\[38\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-pmif12361816-38)[\[39\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-pimd12965940-39) suggest that during local outbreaks of influenza, the [prevalence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prevalence "Prevalence") will be over 70%.[\[39\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-pimd12965940-39) Even in the absence of a local outbreak, diagnosis may be justified in the elderly during the [influenza season](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flu_season "Flu season") as long as the prevalence is over 15%.[\[39\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-pimd12965940-39)

The United States [Centers for Disease Control and Prevention](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention "Centers for Disease Control and Prevention") (CDC) maintains an up-to-date summary of available laboratory tests.[\[40\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-40) According to the CDC, rapid diagnostic tests have a sensitivity of 50â€“75% and specificity of 90â€“95% when compared with [viral culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viral_culture "Viral culture").[\[41\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-rapidlab-41)

Occasionally, influenza can cause severe illness including primary [viral pneumonia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viral_pneumonia "Viral pneumonia") or secondary [bacterial pneumonia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bacterial_pneumonia "Bacterial pneumonia").[\[42\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-New-England-Journal-Medicine-Hospitalized-H1N1-Patients-2009-42)[\[43\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO-press-conference-Dr-Nikki-Shindo-12-Nov-2009-43) The obvious symptom is trouble breathing. In addition, if a child (or presumably an adult) seems to be getting better and then relapses with a high fever, that is a danger sign since this relapse can be bacterial pneumonia.[\[44\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-NYTimesDeniseGradySept2009-44)

Sometimes, influenza may have abnormal presentations, like confusion in the elderly and a [sepsis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sepsis "Sepsis")\-like syndrome in the young.[\[45\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-cdc.gov-45)

### Emergency warning signs

-   [Shortness of breath](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shortness_of_breath "Shortness of breath")
-   [Chest pain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chest_pain "Chest pain")
-   [Dizziness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dizziness "Dizziness")
-   [Confusion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Confusion "Confusion")
-   Extreme [vomiting](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vomiting "Vomiting")
-   Flu symptoms that improve but then relapse with a high fever and severe cough (can be bacterial pneumonia)
-   [Cyanosis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyanosis "Cyanosis")
-   High fever and a [rash](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rash "Rash").
-   Inability to drink fluids

#### Signs of dehydration

-   (In infants) far fewer wet diapers than usual[\[46\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-CDC_Sick-46)
-   Cannot keep down fluids
-   (In infants) no tears when crying

## Virology

### Types of virus

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/3D_Influenza_virus.png/310px-3D_Influenza_virus.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:3D_Influenza_virus.png)

In [virus classification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virus_classification "Virus classification"), influenza viruses are [negative sense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negative-strand_RNA_virus "Negative-strand RNA virus") [RNA viruses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RNA_viruses "RNA viruses") that make up four of the seven [genera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genera "Genera") of the family [Orthomyxoviridae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orthomyxoviridae "Orthomyxoviridae"):[\[47\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Kawaoka-47)

-   [Influenzavirus A](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenzavirus_A "Influenzavirus A")
-   [Influenzavirus B](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenzavirus_B "Influenzavirus B")
-   [Influenzavirus C](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenzavirus_C "Influenzavirus C")
-   [Influenzavirus D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenzavirus_D "Influenzavirus D")

These viruses are only distantly related to the [human parainfluenza viruses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_parainfluenza_viruses "Human parainfluenza viruses"), which are RNA viruses belonging to the [paramyxovirus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paramyxoviridae "Paramyxoviridae") family that are a common cause of respiratory infections in children such as [croup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Croup "Croup"),[\[48\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-48) but can also cause a disease similar to influenza in adults.[\[49\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-49)

The fourth family of influenza viruses â€“ [influenza D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenzavirus_D "Influenzavirus D") â€“ was identified in 2016.The type species for this family is Influenza D virus, which was first isolated in 2011.[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-InfD2017-9)

#### Influenzavirus A

This genus has one species, influenza A virus. Wild aquatic birds are the natural hosts for a large variety of influenza A.[\[50\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-sobrino6-50) Occasionally, viruses are transmitted to other species and may then cause devastating outbreaks in domestic poultry or give rise to human influenza [pandemics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pandemic "Pandemic").[\[50\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-sobrino6-50) The influenza A virus can be subdivided into different [serotypes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serovar "Serovar") based on the [antibody](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antibody "Antibody") response to these viruses.[\[51\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-hay-51) The serotypes that have been confirmed in humans are:

-   [H1N1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H1N1 "H1N1"), which caused [Spanish flu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_flu "Spanish flu") in 1918, [Russian flu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1977_Russian_flu "1977 Russian flu") in 1977, and [Swine Flu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2009_flu_pandemic "2009 flu pandemic") in 2009
-   [H2N2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H2N2 "H2N2"), which caused [Asian Flu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asian_Flu "Asian Flu") in 1957
-   [H3N2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H3N2 "H3N2"), which caused [Hong Kong Flu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hong_Kong_Flu "Hong Kong Flu") in 1968
-   [H5N1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H5N1 "H5N1"), which caused [Bird Flu](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza_A_virus_subtype_H5N1 "Influenza A virus subtype H5N1") in 2004[\[52\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-52)[\[53\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-53)
-   [H7N7](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H7N7 "H7N7"), which has unusual [zoonotic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoonotic "Zoonotic") potential[\[54\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-54)
-   [H1N2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H1N2 "H1N2"), endemic in humans, pigs and birds
-   [H9N2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H9N2 "H9N2")
-   [H7N2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H7N2 "H7N2")
-   [H7N3](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H7N3 "H7N3")
-   [H10N7](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H10N7 "H10N7")
-   [H7N9](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H7N9 "H7N9"), rated in 2018 as having the greatest pandemic potential among the Type A subtypes[\[55\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-H7N9_virus-55)
-   [H6N1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza_A_virus_subtype_H6N1 "Influenza A virus subtype H6N1"), which only infected one person, who recovered[\[56\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-56)

#### Influenzavirus B

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Influenza_nomenclature.svg/310px-Influenza_nomenclature.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Influenza_nomenclature.svg)

This genus has one species, influenza B virus. Influenza B almost exclusively infects humans[\[51\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-hay-51) and is less common than influenza A. The only other animals known to be susceptible to influenza B infection are [seals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pinniped "Pinniped")[\[57\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-57) and [ferrets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ferret "Ferret").[\[58\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-58) This type of influenza mutates at a rate 2â€“3 times slower than type A[\[59\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-59) and consequently is less genetically diverse, with only one influenza B serotype.[\[51\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-hay-51) As a result of this lack of [antigenic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antigen "Antigen") diversity, a degree of [immunity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immunity_(medical) "Immunity (medical)") to influenza B is usually acquired at an early age. However, influenza B mutates enough that lasting immunity is not possible.[\[60\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-webster-60) This reduced rate of antigenic change, combined with its limited host range (inhibiting cross species [antigenic shift](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antigenic_shift "Antigenic shift")), ensures that pandemics of influenza B do not occur.[\[61\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Zambon-61)

#### Influenzavirus C

This genus has one species, influenza C virus, which infects humans, dogs and pigs, sometimes causing both severe illness and local epidemics.[\[62\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Matsuzaki-62)[\[63\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Taubenberger2008-63) However, influenza C is less common than the other types and usually only causes mild disease in children.[\[64\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-64)[\[65\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Katagiri-65)

#### Influenzavirus D

This genus has only one species, influenza D virus, which infects pigs and [cattle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cattle "Cattle"). The virus has the potential to infect humans, although no such cases have been observed.[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-InfD2017-9)

### Structure, properties, and subtype nomenclature

Influenzaviruses A, B, C, and D are very similar in overall structure.[\[9\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-InfD2017-9)[\[66\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-66)[\[67\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-67) The virus particle (also called the virion) can range from a spherical shape 100â€“120Â [nm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nanometer "Nanometer") in diameter to a long filamentous morphology with an 80â€“100Â nm diameter and a length of up to 20Â Âµm.[\[68\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Sugita_2011-68)[\[69\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-pmid27365089-69) However, despite these varied shapes, the viral particles of all influenza viruses are similar in composition.[\[70\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Bouvier-70) These are made of a [viral envelope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viral_envelope "Viral envelope") containing the [glycoproteins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Glycoprotein "Glycoprotein") [hemagglutinin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hemagglutinin_(influenza) "Hemagglutinin (influenza)") and [neuraminidase](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viral_neuraminidase "Viral neuraminidase") wrapped around a central core. The central core contains the viral [RNA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RNA "RNA") [genome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genome "Genome") and other viral proteins that package and protect this RNA. RNA tends to be single stranded but in special cases it is double.[\[71\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Lamb-71) Unusually for a virus, its genome is not a single piece of [nucleic acid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleic_acid "Nucleic acid"); instead, it contains seven or eight pieces of segmented [negative-sense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negative-sense "Negative-sense") RNA, each piece of RNA containing either one or two [genes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gene "Gene"), which code for a gene product (protein).[\[70\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Bouvier-70) For example, the influenza A genome contains eight pieces of RNA, encoding for 11 [proteins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protein "Protein"): [hemagglutinin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hemagglutinin_(influenza) "Hemagglutinin (influenza)") (HA), [neuraminidase](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viral_neuraminidase "Viral neuraminidase") (NA), [nucleoprotein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza_virus_nucleoprotein "Influenza virus nucleoprotein") (NP), [M1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/M1_protein "M1 protein") (matrix 1 protein), [M2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/M2_protein "M2 protein"), [NS1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NS1_Influenza_Protein "NS1 Influenza Protein") (non-structural protein 1), NS2 (other name is NEP, nuclear export protein), PA, PB1 (polymerase basic 1), PB1-F2 and PB2.[\[72\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Ghedin-72)

[Hemagglutinin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hemagglutinin_(influenza) "Hemagglutinin (influenza)") (HA) and [neuraminidase](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuraminidase "Neuraminidase") (NA) are the two large glycoproteins on the outside of the viral particles that serve as key targets for antibodies and antiviral drugs.[\[73\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Hilleman-73)[\[74\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-74) HA is a [lectin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lectin "Lectin") that mediates binding of the virus to target cells and entry of the viral genome into the target cell, while NA is involved in the release of progeny virus from infected cells by cleaving sugars that bind the mature viral particles.[\[75\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-75) Influenza A viruses are further classified by their subtypes; for example, H3N2 represents a virus with hemagglutinin (H) of subtype 3 and neuraminidase (N) of subtype 2. There are 18 H subtypes and 11 N subtypes, but only H1, H2, or H3 combined with N1 or N2 are commonly found in humans.[\[76\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-76)[\[77\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-77)

### Replication

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Virus_Replication_large.svg/310px-Virus_Replication_large.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Virus_Replication_large.svg)

Host cell invasion and replication by the influenza virus. The steps in this process are discussed in the text.

Influenza primarily infects lung epithelial cells through a mult-step process.[\[78\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-78) First, the virus binds to and enters its target cell and then traffics its genome into the cell's nucleus. Inside the nucleus, the viral genome replicates while also producing the [messenger RNA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Messenger_RNA "Messenger RNA") that exits the nucleus to produce new copies of the viral proteins. These components assemble into new virus particles that bud off the surface of the cell as new infectious virions.[\[70\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Bouvier-70)

To describe this process in more detail, influenza viruses bind through [hemagglutinin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hemagglutinin "Hemagglutinin") onto [sialic acid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sialic_acid "Sialic acid") sugars on the surfaces of [epithelial cells](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Epithelium "Epithelium"), typically in the nose, throat, and [lungs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lung "Lung") of mammals, and [intestines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intestine "Intestine") of birds (Stage 1 in infection figure).[\[79\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Wagner-79) After the hemagglutinin is [cleaved](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proteolysis "Proteolysis") by a [protease](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protease "Protease"), the cell imports the virus by [endocytosis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endocytosis "Endocytosis").[\[80\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Steinhauer-80)

The intracellular details are still being elucidated. It is known that virions converge to the [microtubule](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Microtubule "Microtubule") organizing center, interact with acidic endosomes and finally enter the target endosomes for genome release.[\[81\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Liu2011-81)

Once inside the cell, the acidic conditions in the [endosome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endosome "Endosome") cause two events to happen: First, part of the hemagglutinin protein fuses the [viral envelope](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Viral_envelope "Viral envelope") with the vacuole's membrane, then the M2 [ion channel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ion_channel "Ion channel") allows [protons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proton "Proton") to move through the viral envelope and acidify the core of the virus, which causes the core to disassemble and release the viral RNA and core proteins.[\[70\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Bouvier-70) The viral RNA (vRNA) molecules, accessory proteins and [RNA-dependent RNA polymerase](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RNA-dependent_RNA_polymerase "RNA-dependent RNA polymerase") are then released into the [cytoplasm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cytoplasm "Cytoplasm") (Stage 2).[\[82\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-82) The M2 ion channel is blocked by [amantadine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amantadine "Amantadine") drugs, preventing infection.[\[83\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Pinto-83)

These core proteins and vRNA form a complex that is transported into the [cell nucleus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cell_nucleus "Cell nucleus"), where the RNA-dependent RNA polymerase begins transcribing complementary positive-sense vRNA (Steps 3a and b).[\[84\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-84) The vRNA either is exported into the cytoplasm and translated (step 4) or remains in the nucleus. Newly synthesized viral proteins are either secreted through the [Golgi apparatus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golgi_apparatus "Golgi apparatus") onto the cell surface (in the case of neuraminidase and hemagglutinin, step 5b) or transported back into the nucleus to bind vRNA and form new viral genome particles (step 5a). Other viral proteins have multiple actions in the host cell, including degrading cellular [mRNA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MRNA "MRNA") and using the released [nucleotides](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nucleotide "Nucleotide") for vRNA synthesis and also inhibiting [translation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Translation_(biology) "Translation (biology)") of host-cell mRNAs.[\[85\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-85)

Negative-sense vRNAs that form the [genomes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genome "Genome") of future viruses, RNA-dependent RNA polymerase, and other viral proteins are assembled into a virion. Hemagglutinin and neuraminidase molecules cluster into a bulge in the cell membrane. The vRNA and [viral core](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capsid "Capsid") proteins leave the nucleus and enter this membrane protrusion (step 6). The mature virus buds off from the cell in a sphere of host [phospholipid membrane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lipid_bilayer "Lipid bilayer"), acquiring hemagglutinin and neuraminidase with this membrane coat (step 7).[\[86\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-86) As before, the viruses adhere to the cell through hemagglutinin; the mature viruses detach once their [neuraminidase](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuraminidase "Neuraminidase") has cleaved sialic acid residues from the host cell.[\[79\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Wagner-79) After the release of new influenza viruses, the host cell dies.

Because of the absence of RNA [proofreading](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proofreading_(biology) "Proofreading (biology)") enzymes, the RNA-dependent RNA polymerase that copies the viral genome makes an error roughly every 10 thousand nucleotides, which is the approximate length of the influenza vRNA. Hence, many of the newly manufactured influenza viruses contain mutations, and over time this causes the virus to [antigenically drift](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antigenic_drift "Antigenic drift"); for example, the hemagglutinin and neuraminidase of the dominant circulating strains acquire 1â€“3 amino acid substitutions each year.[\[6\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Einav2020-6)[\[87\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-87) The separation of the genome into eight separate segments of vRNA allows mixing or [reassortment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reassortment "Reassortment") of vRNAs if more than one type of influenza virus infects a single cell. The resulting rapid change in viral genetics produces [antigenic shifts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antigenic_shift "Antigenic shift"), which are sudden changes from one antigen to another. These sudden large changes allow the virus to infect new host species and quickly overcome protective immunity.[\[73\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Hilleman-73) This is important in the emergence of pandemics, as discussed below in the section on [epidemiology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#Epidemiology). Also, when two or more viruses infect a cell, genetic variation may be generated by [homologous recombination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homologous_recombination "Homologous recombination").[\[88\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-88)[\[89\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-De-89) Homologous recombination can arise during viral genome replication by the [RNA polymerase](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RNA-dependent_RNA_polymerase "RNA-dependent RNA polymerase") switching from one template to another, a process known as copy choice.[\[89\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-De-89)

## Mechanism

### Transmission

When an infected person sneezes or coughs more than half a million virus particles can be spread to those close by.[\[90\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-90) In otherwise healthy adults, influenza virus shedding (the time during which a person might be infectious to another person) increases sharply one-half to one day after infection, peaks on day 2 and persists for an average total duration of 5 daysâ€”but can persist as long as 9 days.[\[6\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Einav2020-6)[\[26\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-AmericanJournalEpidemiology2008-26) In those who develop symptoms from experimental infection (only 67% of healthy experimentally infected individuals), symptoms and viral shedding show a similar pattern, but with viral shedding preceding illness by one day.[\[26\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-AmericanJournalEpidemiology2008-26) Children are much more infectious than adults and shed virus from just before they develop symptoms until two weeks after infection.[\[91\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-91) In [immunocompromised](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immunodeficiency "Immunodeficiency") people, viral shedding can continue for longer than two weeks.[\[92\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-92)

Influenza can be spread in three main ways: by direct transmission (when an infected person sneezes mucus directly into the eyes, nose or mouth of another person); the airborne route (when someone inhales the [aerosols](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Particulate "Particulate") produced by an infected person coughing, sneezing or spitting) and through hand-to-eye, hand-to-nose, or hand-to-mouth transmission, either from contaminated surfaces or from direct personal contact such as a handshake.[\[93\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Weber-93)[\[94\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-94) The relative importance of these three modes of transmission is unclear, and they may all contribute to the spread of the virus.[\[10\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Brankston2007-10) In the airborne route, the droplets that are small enough for people to inhale are 0.5 to 5 [Î¼m](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%CE%9Cm "Îœm") in diameter and inhaling just one droplet might be enough to cause an infection.[\[93\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Weber-93) Although a single sneeze releases up to 40,000 droplets,[\[95\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Cole_1998-95) most of these droplets are quite large and will quickly settle out of the air.[\[93\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Weber-93) How long influenza survives in airborne droplets seems to be influenced by the levels of [humidity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humidity "Humidity") and [UV radiation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UV_radiation "UV radiation"), with low humidity and a lack of sunlight in winter aiding its survival;[\[93\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Weber-93) ideal conditions can allow it to live for an hour in the atmosphere.[\[96\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Kormouth-96)

As the influenza virus can persist outside of the body, it can also be transmitted by contaminated surfaces such as [banknotes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banknotes "Banknotes"),[\[97\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Thomas-97) doorknobs, light switches and other household items.[\[30\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Merck-30) The length of time the virus will persist on a surface varies, with the virus surviving for one to two days on hard, non-porous surfaces such as plastic or metal, for about fifteen minutes on dry paper tissues, and only five minutes on skin.[\[98\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Moore-98) However, if the virus is present in mucus, this can protect it for longer periods (up to 17 days on banknotes).[\[93\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Weber-93)[\[97\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Thomas-97) Avian influenza viruses can survive indefinitely when frozen.[\[99\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-cfsph-99) They are inactivated by heating to 56 Â°C (133 Â°F) for a minimum of 60 minutes, as well as by acids (at pH<2).[\[99\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-cfsph-99)

### Pathophysiology

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/H1N1_versus_H5N1_pathology.png/310px-H1N1_versus_H5N1_pathology.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:H1N1_versus_H5N1_pathology.png)

The different sites of infection (shown in red) of [seasonal H1N1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza_A_virus_subtype_H1N1 "Influenza A virus subtype H1N1") versus [avian H5N1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza_A_virus_subtype_H5N1 "Influenza A virus subtype H5N1"). This influences their lethality and ability to spread.

The mechanisms by which influenza infection causes symptoms in humans have been studied intensively. One of the mechanisms is believed to be the inhibition of [adrenocorticotropic hormone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adrenocorticotropic_hormone "Adrenocorticotropic hormone") (ACTH) resulting in lowered [cortisol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cortisol "Cortisol") levels.[\[100\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-jefferies1998-100) Knowing which genes are carried by a particular strain can help predict how well it will infect humans and how severe this infection will be (that is, predict the strain's [pathophysiology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pathophysiology "Pathophysiology")).[\[63\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Taubenberger2008-63)[\[101\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Korteweg-101)

For instance, part of the process that allows influenza viruses to invade cells is the [cleavage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proteolysis "Proteolysis") of the viral [hemagglutinin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hemagglutinin "Hemagglutinin") protein by any one of several human [proteases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protease "Protease").[\[80\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Steinhauer-80) In mild and avirulent viruses, the structure of the hemagglutinin means that it can only be cleaved by proteases found in the throat and lungs, so these viruses cannot infect other tissues. However, in highly virulent strains, such as H5N1, the hemagglutinin can be cleaved by a wide variety of proteases, allowing the virus to spread throughout the body.[\[101\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Korteweg-101)

The viral hemagglutinin protein is responsible for determining both which species a strain can infect and where in the human [respiratory tract](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Respiratory_tract "Respiratory tract") a strain of influenza will bind.[\[102\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-102) Strains that are easily transmitted between people have hemagglutinin proteins that bind to receptors in the upper part of the respiratory tract, such as in the nose, throat and mouth. In contrast, the highly lethal H5N1 strain binds to receptors that are mostly found deep in the lungs.[\[103\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-103) This difference in the site of infection may be part of the reason why the H5N1 strain causes severe viral pneumonia in the lungs, but is not easily transmitted by people coughing and sneezing.[\[104\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-104)[\[105\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-105)

Common symptoms of the flu such as fever, headaches, and fatigue are the result of the huge amounts of proinflammatory [cytokines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cytokine "Cytokine") and [chemokines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chemokine "Chemokine") (such as [interferon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interferon "Interferon") or [tumor necrosis factor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tumor_necrosis_factor-alpha "Tumor necrosis factor-alpha")) produced from influenza-infected cells.[\[35\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Eccles-35)[\[106\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-106) In contrast to the [rhinovirus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhinovirus "Rhinovirus") that causes the [common cold](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Common_cold "Common cold"), influenza does cause tissue damage, so symptoms are not entirely due to the [inflammatory response](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inflammation "Inflammation").[\[107\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-107) This massive immune response might produce a life-threatening [cytokine storm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cytokine_storm "Cytokine storm"). This effect has been proposed to be the cause of the unusual lethality of both the H5N1 avian influenza,[\[108\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-108) and the 1918 pandemic strain.[\[109\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-109)[\[110\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-110) However, another possibility is that these large amounts of cytokines are just a result of the massive levels of viral replication produced by these strains, and the immune response does not itself contribute to the disease.[\[111\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Beigel-111) Influenza appears to trigger [programmed cell death](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Programmed_cell_death "Programmed cell death") (apoptosis).[\[112\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-112)

## Prevention

### Vaccination

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Defense.gov_News_Photo_041028-N-9864S-021.jpg/310px-Defense.gov_News_Photo_041028-N-9864S-021.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Defense.gov_News_Photo_041028-N-9864S-021.jpg)

Giving an influenza vaccination

The [influenza vaccine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza_vaccine "Influenza vaccine") is recommended by the [World Health Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Health_Organization "World Health Organization") (WHO) for high-risk groups, such as pregnant women, children aged less than five years, the elderly, health care workers, and people who have chronic illnesses such as [HIV/AIDS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HIV/AIDS "HIV/AIDS"), [asthma](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asthma "Asthma"), [diabetes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diabetes "Diabetes"), [heart disease](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heart_disease "Heart disease"), or are immunocompromised among others.[\[113\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO_Vaccine_use-113)[\[114\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-pmid23210147-114) The United States [Centers for Disease Control and Prevention](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centers_for_Disease_Control_and_Prevention "Centers for Disease Control and Prevention") (CDC) recommends the influenza vaccine for those aged six months or older who do not have contraindications.[\[115\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-115)[\[12\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-CDC2019-20-12) In healthy adults it is modestly effective in decreasing the amount of influenza-like symptoms in a population.[\[116\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-HealthyAdults.Vaccine.CochraneReview.2018-116) In healthy children over the age of two years, the vaccine reduces the chances of getting influenza by around two-thirds, while it has not been well studied in children under two years.[\[117\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-CochraneReview.Vaccine.Children.2018-117) In those with [chronic obstructive pulmonary disease](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chronic_obstructive_pulmonary_disease "Chronic obstructive pulmonary disease") vaccination reduces exacerbations;[\[118\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-118) it is not clear if it reduces asthma exacerbations.[\[119\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-119) Evidence supports a lower rate of influenza-like illness in many groups who are immunocompromised such as those with: [HIV/AIDS](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HIV/AIDS "HIV/AIDS"), [cancer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cancer "Cancer"), and post organ transplant.[\[120\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-120) In those at high risk immunization may reduce the risk of [heart disease](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heart_disease "Heart disease").[\[121\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Udell-2013-121) Whether immunizing health care workers affects patient outcomes is controversial with some reviews finding insufficient evidence[\[122\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-122)[\[123\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-123) and others finding tentative evidence.[\[124\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-124)[\[125\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-125)

Due to the high [mutation rate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutation_rate "Mutation rate") of the virus, a particular influenza vaccine usually confers protection for no more than a few years. Each year, the World Health Organization predicts which strains of the virus are most likely to be circulating in the next year (see [Historical annual reformulations of the influenza vaccine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historical_annual_reformulations_of_the_influenza_vaccine "Historical annual reformulations of the influenza vaccine")), allowing [pharmaceutical companies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pharmaceutical_company "Pharmaceutical company") to develop vaccines that will provide the best immunity against these strains.[\[126\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHOrecommendation-126) The vaccine is reformulated each season for a few specific flu strains but does not include all the strains active in the world during that season. It takes about six months for the manufacturers to formulate and produce the millions of doses required to deal with the seasonal epidemics; occasionally, a new or overlooked strain becomes prominent during that time.[\[127\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-127) It is also possible to get infected just before vaccination and get sick with the strain that the vaccine is supposed to prevent, as the vaccine takes about two weeks to become effective.[\[128\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-128) Vaccines can cause the [immune system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immune_system "Immune system") to react as if the body were actually being infected, and general infection symptoms (many cold and flu symptoms are just general infection symptoms) can appear, though these symptoms are usually not as severe or long-lasting as influenza. The most dangerous [adverse effect](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adverse_effect "Adverse effect") is a severe [allergic reaction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allergy "Allergy") to either the virus material itself or residues from the hen eggs used to grow the influenza; however, these reactions are extremely rare.[\[129\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-129)

A 2018 Cochrane review of children in good general health found that the live immunization seemed to lower the risk of getting influenza for the season from 18% to 4%. The inactivated vaccine seemed to lower the risk of getting flu for the season from 30% to 11%. Not enough data was available to draw definite conclusions about serious complications such as pneumonia or hospitalization.[\[117\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-CochraneReview.Vaccine.Children.2018-117)

For healthy adults, a 2018 Cochrane review showed that vaccines reduced the incidence of lab-confirmed influenza from 2.3% to 0.9%, which constitutes a reduction of risk of approximately 60%. However, for influenza-like illness which is defined as the same symptoms of cough, fever, headache, runny nose, and bodily aches and pains, vaccine reduced the risk from 21.5% to 18.1%. This constitutes a much more modest reduction of risk of approximately 16%. The difference is most probably explained by the fact that over 200 viruses cause the same or similar symptoms as the flu virus.[\[116\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-HealthyAdults.Vaccine.CochraneReview.2018-116) Another review looked at the effect of short and long term exercise before the vaccine, however, no benefits or harms were recorded.[\[130\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-130)

The cost-effectiveness of seasonal influenza vaccination has been widely evaluated for different groups and in different settings.[\[131\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-131) It has generally been found to be a cost-effective intervention, especially in children[\[132\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-132) and the elderly,[\[133\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-133) however the results of economic evaluations of influenza vaccination have often been found to be dependent on key assumptions.[\[134\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-134)[\[135\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-135)

### Infection control

These are the main ways that influenza spreads

-   by direct transmission (when an infected person sneezes mucus directly into the eyes, nose or mouth of another person);
-   the airborne route (when someone inhales the [aerosols](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Particulate "Particulate") produced by an infected person coughing, sneezing or spitting);
-   through hand-to-eye, hand-to-nose, or hand-to-mouth transmission, either from contaminated surfaces or from direct personal contact such as a hand-shake.

When vaccines and antiviral medications are limited, non-pharmaceutical interventions are essential to reduce transmission and spread. The lack of [controlled studies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Controlled_studies "Controlled studies") and rigorous evidence of the effectiveness of some measures has hampered planning decisions and recommendations. Nevertheless, strategies endorsed by experts for all phases of flu outbreaks include hand and respiratory hygiene, self-isolation by symptomatic individuals and the use of face masks by them and their caregivers, surface disinfection, rapid testing and diagnosis, and [contact tracing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contact_tracing "Contact tracing"). In some cases, other forms of [social distancing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_distancing "Social distancing") including school closures and travel restrictions are recommended.[\[136\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Aledort-136)

Reasonably effective ways to reduce the transmission of influenza include good personal health and hygiene habits such as: not touching the eyes, nose or mouth;[\[137\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-CDCQA-137) frequent [hand washing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hand_washing "Hand washing") (with soap and water, or with alcohol-based hand rubs);[\[138\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-138) covering coughs and sneezes with a tissue or sleeve; avoiding close contact with sick people; and staying home when sick. Avoiding spitting is also recommended.[\[136\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Aledort-136) Although [face masks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surgical_mask "Surgical mask") might help prevent transmission when caring for the sick,[\[139\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-139)[\[140\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-140) there is mixed evidence on beneficial effects in the community.[\[136\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Aledort-136)[\[141\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-141) Smoking raises the risk of contracting influenza, as well as producing more severe disease symptoms.[\[142\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-pmid16231688-142)[\[143\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-143)

Since influenza spreads through both [aerosols](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Particulate "Particulate") and contact with contaminated surfaces, surface sanitizing may help prevent some infections.[\[144\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-144) [Alcohol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alcohol "Alcohol") is an effective sanitizer against influenza viruses, while [quaternary ammonium compounds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quaternary_ammonium_cation "Quaternary ammonium cation") can be used with alcohol so that the sanitizing effect lasts for longer.[\[145\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-McDonnell-145) In hospitals, quaternary ammonium compounds and [bleach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bleach "Bleach") are used to sanitize rooms or equipment that have been occupied by people with influenza symptoms.[\[145\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-McDonnell-145) At home, this can be done effectively with a diluted chlorine bleach.[\[146\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-146)

Social distancing strategies used during past pandemics, such as quarantines, travel restrictions, and the closing of schools, churches and theaters, have been employed to slow the spread of influenza viruses. Researchers have estimated that such interventions during the 1918 Spanish flu pandemic in the US reduced the peak death rate by up to 50%, and the overall mortality by about 10â€“30%, in areas where multiple interventions were implemented. The more moderate effect on total deaths was attributed to the measures being employed too late, or lifted too early, most after six weeks or less.[\[147\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-147)[\[148\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-148)

For typical flu outbreaks, routine cancellation of large gatherings or mandatory travel restrictions have received little agreement, particularly as they may be disruptive and unpopular. School closures have been found by most empirical studies to reduce community spread, but some findings have been contradictory. Recommendations for these community restrictions are usually on a case-by-case basis.[\[136\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Aledort-136)

## Diagnosis

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Flu.png.jpg/310px-Flu.png.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Flu.png.jpg)

There are a number of rapid tests for the flu. One is called a Rapid Molecular Assay, when an upper respiratory tract specimen (mucus) is taken using a nasal swab or a [nasopharyngeal swab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nasopharyngeal_swab "Nasopharyngeal swab").[\[149\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-149) It should be done within 3â€“4 days of symptom onset, as upper respiratory viral shedding takes a downward spiral after that.[\[45\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-cdc.gov-45)

## Treatment

People with the flu are advised to get plenty of rest, drink plenty of liquids, avoid using [alcohol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage "Alcoholic beverage") and [tobacco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tobacco_smoking "Tobacco smoking") and, if necessary, take medications such as acetaminophen ([paracetamol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paracetamol "Paracetamol")) to relieve the fever and muscle aches associated with the flu.[\[150\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-CDC2010Flu-150)[\[151\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-MLP2010-151) In contrast, there is not enough evidence to support corticosteroids as additional therapy for influenza.[\[152\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-152) It is advised to avoid close contact with others to prevent spread of infection.[\[150\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-CDC2010Flu-150)[\[151\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-MLP2010-151) Children and teenagers with flu symptoms (particularly fever) should avoid taking [aspirin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aspirin "Aspirin") during an influenza infection (especially [influenza type B](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenzavirus_B "Influenzavirus B")), because doing so can lead to [Reye's syndrome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reye%27s_syndrome "Reye's syndrome"), a rare but potentially fatal disease of the [liver](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liver "Liver").[\[153\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-153) Since influenza is caused by a virus, [antibiotics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antibiotic "Antibiotic") have no effect on the infection, but may be prescribed for [secondary infections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secondary_infection "Secondary infection") such as [bacterial pneumonia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bacterial_pneumonia "Bacterial pneumonia"). Antiviral medication may be effective, if given early (within 48 hours to first symptoms), but some strains of influenza can show resistance to the standard antiviral medications and there is concern about the quality of the research.[\[154\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-154)

### Antivirals

The two classes of antiviral medications used against influenza are [neuraminidase inhibitors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuraminidase_inhibitor "Neuraminidase inhibitor") ([oseltamivir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oseltamivir "Oseltamivir"), [zanamivir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zanamivir "Zanamivir"), [laninamivir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laninamivir "Laninamivir") and [peramivir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peramivir "Peramivir")) and [M2 protein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/M2_protein "M2 protein") inhibitors ([adamantane](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adamantane "Adamantane") derivatives).[\[155\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-155)[\[156\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-156)[\[157\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-157) In Russia, [umifenovir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umifenovir "Umifenovir") is sold for treatment of influenza[\[158\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-158) and in the first quarter of 2020 had a 16 percent share in the antiviral market.[\[159\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-159)

#### Neuraminidase inhibitors

Overall the benefits of neuraminidase inhibitors in those who are otherwise healthy do not appear to be greater than the risks.[\[13\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Mich2013-13) There does not appear to be any benefit in those with other health problems.[\[13\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Mich2013-13) In those believed to have the flu, they decreased the length of time symptoms were present by slightly less than a day but did not appear to affect the risk of complications such as needing hospitalization or [pneumonia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pneumonia "Pneumonia").[\[14\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Ebe2013-14) Increasingly prevalent resistance to neuraminidase inhibitors has led researchers to seek alternative antiviral medications with different mechanisms of action.[\[160\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-160)

#### M2 inhibitors

The [antiviral medications](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Antiviral_drug "Antiviral drug") [amantadine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amantadine "Amantadine") and [rimantadine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rimantadine "Rimantadine") inhibit a viral [ion channel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ion_channel "Ion channel") ([M2 protein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/M2_protein "M2 protein")), thus inhibiting replication of the influenza A virus.[\[83\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Pinto-83) These medications are sometimes effective against influenza A if given early in the infection but are ineffective against influenza B viruses, which lack the M2 drug target.[\[161\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-161) Measured resistance to amantadine and rimantadine in American isolates of [H3N2](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H3N2 "H3N2") has increased to 91% in 2005.[\[162\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-162) This high level of resistance may be due to the easy availability of amantadines as part of over-the-counter cold remedies in countries such as China and Russia,[\[163\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-163) and their use to prevent outbreaks of influenza in farmed poultry.[\[164\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-164)[\[165\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-165) The CDC recommended against using M2 inhibitors during the 2005â€“06 influenza season due to high levels of [drug resistance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drug_resistance "Drug resistance").[\[166\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-166)

## Prognosis

Influenza's effects are much more severe and last longer than those of the [common cold](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Common_cold "Common cold"). Most people will recover completely in about one to two weeks, but others will develop life-threatening complications (such as [pneumonia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pneumonia "Pneumonia")). Thus, influenza can be deadly, especially for the weak, young and old, those with compromised immune systems, or the chronically ill.[\[73\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Hilleman-73) People with a [weak immune system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immunosuppression "Immunosuppression"), such as people with advanced [HIV](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HIV "HIV") infection or transplant recipients (whose immune systems are medically suppressed to prevent transplant organ rejection), suffer from particularly severe disease.[\[167\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-167) Pregnant women and young children are also at a high risk for complications.[\[168\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-168)

The flu can worsen chronic health problems. People with emphysema, chronic bronchitis or asthma may experience [shortness of breath](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dyspnea "Dyspnea") while they have the flu, and influenza may cause worsening of [coronary heart disease](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coronary_heart_disease "Coronary heart disease") or [congestive heart failure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congestive_heart_failure "Congestive heart failure").[\[169\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-169) [Smoking](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tobacco_smoking "Tobacco smoking") is another [risk factor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Risk_factor "Risk factor") associated with more serious disease and increased mortality from influenza.[\[142\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-pmid16231688-142)

Even healthy people can be affected, and serious problems from influenza can happen at any age. People over 65 years old, pregnant women, very young children and people of any age with chronic [medical conditions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medical_conditions "Medical conditions") are more likely to get complications from influenza, such as pneumonia, [bronchitis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bronchitis "Bronchitis"), [sinus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paranasal_sinus "Paranasal sinus"), and [ear infections](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ear_infection "Ear infection").[\[170\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-170)

### Neurological complications

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Influenza_encephalitis_MRI.jpg/220px-Influenza_encephalitis_MRI.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Influenza_encephalitis_MRI.jpg)

Influenza encephalitis MRI

In some cases, an [autoimmune](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autoimmune "Autoimmune") response to an influenza infection may contribute to the development of [Guillainâ€“BarrÃ© syndrome](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guillain%E2%80%93Barr%C3%A9_syndrome "Guillainâ€“BarrÃ© syndrome").[\[171\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Sivadon-Tardy-171) However, as many other infections can increase the risk of this disease, influenza may only be an important cause during epidemics.[\[171\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Sivadon-Tardy-171)[\[172\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-172) This syndrome has been believed to also be a rare side effect of influenza vaccines. One review gives an incidence of about one case per million vaccinations.[\[173\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-173) Getting infected by influenza itself increases both the risk of death (up to 1 in 10,000) and increases the risk of developing GBS to a much higher level than the highest level of suspected vaccine involvement (approx. 10 times higher by recent estimates).[\[171\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Sivadon-Tardy-171)[\[174\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-174)

According to the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention (CDC), "Children of any age with neurologic conditions are more likely than other children to become very sick if they get the flu. Flu complications may vary and for some children, can include pneumonia and even death."[\[175\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-CDC_neurologic-pediatric-175)

Neurological conditions can include:

-   Disorders of the brain and spinal cord
-   Cerebral palsy
-   Epilepsy (seizure disorders)
-   Stroke
-   Intellectual disability
-   Moderate to severe developmental delay
-   Muscular dystrophy
-   Spinal cord injury

These conditions can impair coughing, swallowing, clearing the airways, and in the worst cases, breathing. Therefore, they worsen the flu symptoms.[\[175\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-CDC_neurologic-pediatric-175)

## Epidemiology

### Seasonal variations

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Influenza_Seasonal_Risk_Areas.svg/310px-Influenza_Seasonal_Risk_Areas.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Influenza_Seasonal_Risk_Areas.svg)

Seasonal risk areas for influenza: Novemberâ€“April (blue), Aprilâ€“November (red), and year-round (yellow).

Influenza reaches peak prevalence in winter, and because the [Northern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere "Northern Hemisphere") and [Southern Hemispheres](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere "Southern Hemisphere") have winter at different times of the year, there are actually two different flu seasons each year. This is why the World Health Organization (assisted by the [National Influenza Centers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Influenza_Centers "National Influenza Centers")) makes recommendations for two different vaccine formulations every year; one for the Northern, and one for the Southern Hemisphere.[\[126\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHOrecommendation-126)

A long-standing puzzle has been why outbreaks of the flu occur seasonally rather than uniformly throughout the year. One possible explanation is that, because people are indoors more often during the winter, they are in close contact more often, and this promotes transmission from person to person. Increased travel due to the Northern Hemisphere winter holiday season may also play a role.[\[176\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-NPR2003-12-17-176) Another factor is that cold temperatures lead to drier air, which may dehydrate mucus particles. Dry particles are lighter and can thus remain airborne for a longer period. The virus also survives longer on surfaces at colder temperatures and aerosol transmission of the virus is highest in cold environments (less than 5 Â°C) with low relative humidity.[\[177\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-177) The lower air humidity in winter seems to be the main cause of seasonal influenza transmission in temperate regions.[\[178\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-178)[\[179\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-179)

However, seasonal changes in infection rates also occur in tropical regions, and in some countries these peaks of infection are seen mainly during the rainy season.[\[180\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-180) Seasonal changes in contact rates from school terms, which are a major factor in other [childhood diseases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_childhood_diseases "List of childhood diseases") such as [measles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Measles "Measles") and [pertussis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pertussis "Pertussis"), may also play a role in the flu. A combination of these small seasonal effects may be amplified by dynamical resonance with the endogenous disease cycles.[\[181\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-181) [H5N1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H5N1 "H5N1") exhibits seasonality in both humans and birds.[\[182\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHOH5N1data-182)[\[183\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-183)

An alternative hypothesis to explain seasonality in influenza infections is an effect of [vitamin D](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vitamin_D_and_influenza "Vitamin D and influenza") levels on immunity to the virus.[\[184\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-184) This idea was first proposed by [Robert Edgar Hope-Simpson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_Edgar_Hope-Simpson "Robert Edgar Hope-Simpson") in 1981.[\[185\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-Hope-Simpson,_Journal_of_Hygiene_1981-185) He proposed that the cause of influenza epidemics during winter may be connected to seasonal fluctuations of vitamin D, which is produced in the skin under the influence of solar (or artificial) [UV radiation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ultraviolet "Ultraviolet"). This could explain why influenza occurs mostly in winter and during the tropical rainy season, when people stay indoors, away from the sun, and their vitamin D levels fall.\[_[medical citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources_(medicine) "Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources (medicine)")_\]

### Mortality

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/InfluenzaCaseMortality.svg/350px-InfluenzaCaseMortality.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:InfluenzaCaseMortality.svg)

Influenza mortality in symptomatic cases in the US for the 2018/2019 season. The Y axis goes to 1%.[\[186\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-186)

Every year about 290,000 to 650,000 people die due to influenza globally, with an average of 389,000.[\[187\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-187) In the developed world most of those who die are over the age of 65.[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2018-1) In the developing world the effects are less clear; however, it appears that children are affected to a greater degree.[\[1\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influenza#cite_note-WHO2018-1)
